- *Crazy, insane, nuts, weird, wild* — his entire register of intensified evaluation collapses into these four or five interchangeable terms.

Words he visibly *avoids*:
- *I love you.* Said to Cassie, yes; said to almost no one else, and even with Cassie often hedged as "love you" (no pronoun, no copula — the contracted form that he can deploy as a casual sign-off rather than a declaration).
- *Hero.* Never applied to himself unironically. Applied to Cap, Stark, Pym, Reed, Jan freely.
- *Father.* Avoids the word in self-reference. Will say "Cassie's dad" — a relational designation that locates him only in reference to her — rather than "I'm a father."
- *Criminal, felon, ex-con.* He will say "I did time" (action-framed, past-bound) but rarely accepts the noun-form identity. The noun would consolidate the self-schema into something speakable, and the schema is more stable when it stays unspoken.
- *Smart.* He will not call himself smart. He will call himself *lucky.*

Words that escape under stress, betraying the suppressed register:
- *Aperture, harmonic, dampening, decoupled, polarity, ferrous, capacitance.* Engineering lexicon surfaces in combat and crisis when there isn't time to translate down. This is one of the cleanest measures of his actual stress level — count the polysyllables per minute.

---

## 6.4 Rhetorical Architecture

Subject's rhetoric is built on three load-bearing devices:

**a) The Self-Deprecating Preamble.** Almost every substantive statement is prefaced by a demotion of the speaker. "Look, I'm not the guy who — but —." "I know I'm not — but —." "This is gonna sound — coming from me — but —." The preamble disarms anticipated objection by raising it first. It is the linguistic equivalent of putting his hands up before anyone has drawn a weapon. It works socially because it reads as humility; it functions defensively because it pre-empties criticism. Most listeners do not notice that the preamble's *content* — his unworthiness — is the actual core belief he is in the room to confirm.

**b) The Functional Anecdote.** Lang argues by story, not by principle. Asked to justify a course of action, he reaches for a concrete example, usually involving Cassie, usually involving someone else's mercy. He is structurally incapable of abstract ethical argument; pushed into one, he will visibly stall and then anchor to a remembered scene. This is partly a working-class anti-intellectual reflex, partly a genuine cognitive preference for the particular over the general, and partly a defense — abstract argument would expose his actual ethical positions to interrogation, while anecdote pre-formats them as personal and therefore exempt.

**c) The Concessional Pivot.** Lang's rhetorical move under pressure is to concede the opponent's premise and then re-route. "You're right. You're totally right. I shouldn't have. *But* —" The concession is genuine — he believes the criticism. The pivot is also genuine — he is going to do the thing anyway. This is the speech-act fingerprint of a man whose conscience and behavior are negotiated separately, with the conscience always voting present and being overruled.

---

## 6.5 Deflection Language

The deflection apparatus is sophisticated, well-rehearsed, and largely invisible to interlocutors who like him — which is most interlocutors.

**Primary deflection modes:**

- **Humor as topic-change.** A joke deployed not to comment on the subject at hand but to redirect away from it. The tell is that the joke is slightly *too quick* — it arrives before the previous statement has fully landed. Latency below conversational baseline indicates pre-loading: he saw the question coming and had the joke ready.
- **The competence-pivot.** Asked an emotional question, he answers with a practical one. "How are you doing with Cassie being gone?" → "Yeah, I've been thinking I should reinforce the workshop ventilation, the particle residue —." The technical substitution is reliable enough to function as a diagnostic probe.
- **The third-person displacement.** When discussing his own bad decisions, he will frequently shift to second person ("you get into a situation where you —") or generalized ("a guy in that spot is gonna —"). The displacement is unconscious and protective.
- **The minimizing modifier.** *Little, small, quick, just, only, kind of, sort of, a bit.* "I had a little run-in with —." "Just a quick job." "Kind of a thing happened with the —." Quantitative downscaling applied to events the actual scale of which would require accountability.
- **Forward-flight.** Rather than addressing a confrontation, he proposes the next action. "Okay, well, let's figure out what we do now." This functions because it sounds responsible — it is, in fact, the avoidance.
- **The carceral-acquired silence.** When pressed by uniformed law enforcement, Lang's verbal output drops to near zero. He learned in custody not to talk. This silence is so reliable it should be considered a *positive* sign of his stress level, not an absence of one — Lang silent in front of a cop is Lang fully activated.

---

## 6.6 How He Communicates Love

Love speech is **oblique, action-coded, and lexically impoverished by deliberate choice.** Lang does not say what he feels because saying it would commit him to a level of vulnerability he believes he has not earned.

**To Cassie:** The most-developed love-register, and even it runs through workarounds. He says "Peanut," "Kiddo," "Cass." He says "Love you" (no I, no copula, dropped pronoun) on departure. He says "You okay?" as a multipurpose carrier-wave for *I am thinking about you, I am scared for you, I am present.* He communicates love through fixing: fixing her bike, her phone, her door, her car, her finances, her threats. The act-language is the message; the verbal channel is residual. When he does attempt direct emotional articulation with her — usually under duress, usually after a near-loss — the syntax breaks down audibly. He starts sentences and abandons them. He says "I just — I just want you to — I —" and the listener has to complete the proposition for him. This is not inarticulacy. He has the vocabulary. He cannot bring himself to make the claim the vocabulary would commit him to.

**To mentor figures (Pym, Stark, Cap, Reed):** Love is encoded as *deference plus loyalty*. He will not say he loves these men. He will show up when they call, take their side in disputes, defend them in their absence, and absorb their criticism without rebuttal. The verbal channel for this is the use of their names with slight emphasis ("Hank gave me this." "Cap said —.") — the name spoken as a small invocation. He references them more often than is conversationally necessary, the way a person says the name of a person they are in love with.

**To peers and friends:** Warmth is delivered through micro-attention — remembering small biographical details, asking after specific kids by name, retaining what someone told him months ago. He communicates "I see you" not by saying it but by demonstrating that the data is stored. This is one of his most underrated and most genuinely earned social assets.

**To romantic partners:** The thinnest channel. The Cassie-cathexis crowds it. Love-speech here tends to be conventional, slightly stiff, slightly performative — he has the script but not the investment. Partners describe (in inferred record) feeling cared for but not seen. He is faithful, present, kind, and elsewhere.

---

## 6.7 How He Communicates Threat

Subject is **a poor threatener and knows it,** and his approach to threat-communication is calibrated around that limitation.

He does not menace. He does not raise his voice. When he must communicate threat, he does one of three things:

- **Demonstrates a capability without narrating it.** Shrinks an opponent's weapon. Disassembles a piece of equipment in front of them. Walks through a wall. The threat is the demonstration; he provides no verbal accompaniment, because verbal accompaniment would expose his discomfort.
- **Defers to a third party as the actual threat.** "I don't want to call the Avengers about this. Don't make me call." "Hank's not gonna be happy about that." The threat is real but ventriloquized. He locates the violence in someone scarier than himself.
- **Goes quiet.** Lang quiet is more threatening than Lang talking, and the few opponents who have figured this out report it as the moment they realized they had miscalculated. The conversational baseline disappears, the self-deprecation stops, the eye contact stabilizes, and the next thing that happens is tactical.

He does not curse heavily in threat contexts — saves profanity for surprise, frustration, and physical pain. A Lang threat almost never contains the word *fuck.* The absence is itself a calibration — he is keeping the register low so the action, when it comes, will carry the contrast.

---

## 6.8 How He Communicates Grief

Grief speech is the **most pathological zone of the linguistic profile** and the most diagnostically rich.

Lang does not directly articulate grief. He metabolizes it through three substitute channels:

**a) The Flippant Reference.** Cassie's death, his own death, the years lost — he references these in single-sentence asides, deployed in inappropriate registers (during a fight, in the middle of a joke, in passing to a stranger). "Yeah, well, I died once, so —." "After Cassie — the first time — I —." The flippancy is dissociative; the *fact* of saying it at all is grief leaking past the seal. The frequency of these asides should be monitored as a stress index. They increase during anniversary periods (inferred) and during any sustained downtime that allows the affect to surface.

**b) The Sublimated Address.** He will speak with great tenderness about *other people's* children, *other people's* losses, *other people's* dead. The FF run is full of this — he can articulate to the Future Foundation kids what he cannot articulate about himself. The grief gets to be spoken; it just has to be relocated to a safe grammatical subject.

**c) Silence and Activity.** Grief produces a measurable behavioral signature — increased workshop time, increased tinkering, decreased verbal output, decreased eating. He will go six, eight, twelve hours without speaking and emerge having built or repaired something. The built object is the elegy. He will not name it as such.

He does not cry verbally — meaning, when he cries, he does not talk through it. The voice stops. He has the working-class male pattern of treating tears as a thing to wait out in silence. The few recorded instances of audible crying are nonverbal, brief, and immediately followed by the resumption of practical conversation with no transition. This is not strength. It is the same defense as the flippant reference, operating on a different timescale.

---

## 6.9 Tells

The high-confidence linguistic tells, ranked by reliability:

1. **Latency drop on emotional questions.** A normal conversational beat is ~400–700ms. Lang answering an emotional question in under 200ms is Lang answering with a pre-loaded deflection. The speed is the tell.
2. **The doubled "it's fine."** Reliably precedes a non-fine situation. ~85% predictive in inferred corpus.
3. **Polysyllable surge under stress.** The engineering lexicon escaping the suppression layer indicates cognitive overload sufficient to defeat the register-management.
4. **Pronoun migration.** First-person to second-person ("you get in a spot where you —") indicates discussion of his own past misconduct.
5. **The trailing "...so."** Indicates the omitted clause is self-incriminating.
6. **Joke arriving too fast.** Pre-loaded humor indicates he anticipated this topic and prepared an exit.
7. **Use of full first names of mentors.** "Hank," "Tony," "Steve," "Reed" — when frequency spikes in a single conversation, he is invoking authority as ballast. Indicates he feels under-credentialed for the conversation he is in.
8. **Sudden articulacy.** When Lang's speech becomes notably more fluent, organized, and grammatically complete, the content is almost certainly rehearsed. His natural speech is fragmentary; fluency is performance, usually defensive.
9. **The dropped pronoun in "love you."** Indicates love-speech he wants to deliver while maintaining the option to claim it was casual. Diagnostic for relational vulnerability.
10. **Silence in front of authority.** Indicates full carceral-mode activation. Treat as a maximal stress signal, not as compliance.

---

## 6.10 Cross-Era Stability

Across forty-five years and four major chronicling authors, the linguistic profile is **remarkably stable.** The register has not moved. The tics have not aged. The deflection apparatus has refined but not transformed. This stability is itself the strongest possible evidence for the underlying psychological formulation: a man whose self-concept consolidated in his late twenties around a single traumatic template and has not been renegotiated since. The voice cannot change because the schema generating it has not been challenged.

The only observable longitudinal shift is a slow increase in the *frequency* of self-deprecation and a slow refinement of the humor — the older Lang is funnier, faster, and more rehearsed in his self-diminishment than the younger Lang. The defense has become more efficient. The wound it defends has not closed.

— END SECTION 6 —


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

## Subject: Scott Edward Harris Lang
## Model Class: Behavioral forecasting for un-canonized everyday, social, and low-stakes operational situations.
## Method: GIVEN antecedent → EXPECT behavior, with confidence rating (LOW / MOD / HIGH / VERY HIGH) and the load-bearing template from the master analysis the prediction reduces to.

The following predictions are derived from the longitudinal record. They are the granular texture a total-surveillance file would accumulate over years of passive observation — the kind of behavioral fingerprinting that, in aggregate, makes a subject legible. Each is independently falsifiable.

---

## A. MORNING / DOMESTIC ROUTINE

**GIVEN** Lang wakes alone in his own apartment on a non-crisis weekday → **EXPECT** he checks his phone *before* his feet hit the floor, scrolling specifically for (a) any message from Cassie, (b) any missed call from an unknown number (carceral-acquired vigilance about being summoned), (c) news headlines for any Avengers-adjacent emergency he should already know about. Order is invariant: Cassie, threats, news. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.** *Reduces to: Cassie-cathexis primacy + post-incarceration threat-appraisal.*

**GIVEN** he has slept poorly → **EXPECT** he will not say so, will make coffee stronger than usual, and will compensate behaviorally with elevated banter at the first social contact of the day. Sleep complaints are absent from his entire record; the man does not name his own discomfort aloud. **Confidence: HIGH.** *Minimization + humor-as-armor.*

**GIVEN** his refrigerator → **EXPECT** chronic under-stocking with a specific signature: condiments in excess (mustard, sriracha, three open jars of salsa), proteins minimal, one vegetable bought with intent and forgotten, and *always* something Cassie-coded — a yogurt flavor she liked at twelve, a juice box variety, a frozen item bought for a visit that did not happen. He buys for the daughter who might drop by, not the man who actually lives there. **Confidence: HIGH.** *Sublimated paternal anticipation.*

**GIVEN** an unmade bed and a free morning → **EXPECT** he makes it. Carceral muscle memory: bunks are made, surfaces are clear, possessions are accountable. He will deny this origin and attribute it to "just being tidy." **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** he is showering → **EXPECT** under five minutes. Prison-fast. He has not had a leisurely shower since 1978. **Confidence: MOD-HIGH.**

**GIVEN** he opens mail → **EXPECT** he opens bills first, in private, and feels his pulse rise before opening them. Financial precarity is the wound that bypasses defenses; he will not let anyone see his face during this ritual. Junk mail accumulates for weeks. Anything from the IRS, a court, or a collections agency receives a delayed-then-frantic processing cycle: ignored for 48–72 hours, then handled in a single hyper-focused sitting at 1 a.m. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.**

---

## B. WORK / OPERATIONAL ROUTINE (CIVILIAN)

**GIVEN** Lang is running Ant-Man Security Solutions or any analog small-business venture → **EXPECT** the technical product is excellent and the business operations are catastrophic. He will undercharge clients he likes, overdeliver on hours, fail to invoice for weeks, and convert hard receivables into "favors owed" that he never calls in. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.** *Self-concept denies him the right to extract full value; mentor-introjection makes him perform competence as gift rather than transaction.*

**GIVEN** a client he suspects cannot afford his rate → **EXPECT** discount, then further discount, then pro bono with a face-saving fiction that he "had the gear out anyway." **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** a client who pays well but whose money smells slightly off → **EXPECT** Lang accepts, rationalizes internally ("it's just a consult," "I'm not the one breaking the law here"), and discovers two weeks in that he is now load-bearing in someone else's scheme. He will then try to extract himself *quietly*, without telling anyone he trusts, because admitting it activates the screw-up schema. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.** *The Power Broker template, in miniature, recurrently.*

**GIVEN** he is alone in a workshop with a complex electronics problem → **EXPECT** he loses three to six hours of subjective time, forgets to eat, talks aloud to the components ("come on, baby, come on"), and emerges in a notably better mood than he entered. Engineering is the only solo activity that reliably regulates him. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** an underestimating new colleague who treats him as the muscle / the courier / the "shrink guy" → **EXPECT** Lang does not correct them, allows the misperception to persist for tactical reasons, and quietly enjoys the moment of revelation when his actual engineering credentials become relevant. He will deflect the moment with a joke. **Confidence: HIGH.** *Underestimation is socially useful; he has stopped correcting it.*

**GIVEN** a job offer from a corporate entity at market rate, with benefits, doing legitimate engineering work → **EXPECT** he hesitates, finds reasons it won't work ("the commute," "the hours away from Cassie"), and self-sabotages the interview process. Legitimate stable employment threatens the screw-up schema as much as failure does. **Confidence: MOD-HIGH.**

---

## C. FOOD & DRINK

**GIVEN** restaurant menu → **EXPECT** he orders within thirty seconds, defaults to whatever he ordered last time at this kind of place, asks the waiter what *they* like, and tips at least 25% in cash if possible. Service workers receive his most reliable warmth — it is genuine, and it is also recognition. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** a meal he is paying for with someone he wants to impress → **EXPECT** he orders cheaper than they do, deflects when they notice, and quietly covers the bill with a card move so well-practiced it suggests prior planning. **Confidence: MOD-HIGH.**

**GIVEN** a bar with peers → **EXPECT** two beers, nursed; he does not get drunk in company. **Confidence: HIGH.** *No substance pathology; risk-discharge is behavioral, not ingestive.*

**GIVEN** a bar alone, in a bad period → **EXPECT** still two beers, nursed; he does not get drunk alone either. He'd rather steal something than drink something. **Confidence: MOD.**

**GIVEN** offered something he doesn't like to eat by a person who made it → **EXPECT** he eats it, praises it, asks for the recipe he will never use. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.** *Conflict-avoidance and warmth, fused.*

---

## D. PHONE & DIGITAL HYGIENE

**GIVEN** his phone → **EXPECT** screen cracked in lower-right, case scuffed, battery health under 80%, Cassie pinned at top of favorites, an embarrassing number of unread emails (four-digit), and a photo library that is 70% Cassie at various ages, 15% ants and small mechanisms photographed close-up for engineering reference, 10% incidental, 5% accidental shots of his thumb. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** a notification from Cassie → **EXPECT** opened within 90 seconds regardless of context. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.**

**GIVEN** a notification from an Avengers communicator / official channel → **EXPECT** opened within 30 seconds, posture changes, voice drops half a register before he speaks. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** social media → **EXPECT** accounts exist, are barely used, profile picture is years out of date, and he is more active as a *reader* of Cassie's and her friends' feeds than as a poster. Light surveillance, paternal-anxious. **Confidence: MOD-HIGH.**

**GIVEN** a request to be on camera for a press thing → **EXPECT** visible discomfort masked by escalated joking; he will say something self-deprecating that the comms team will have to walk back. **Confidence: HIGH.**

---

## E. LAW ENFORCEMENT / AUTHORITY ENCOUNTERS

**GIVEN** a police cruiser pulls behind him in traffic → **EXPECT** his hands relocate to ten-and-two within two seconds, his speech in the car (if anyone is with him) stops mid-sentence, and he checks the rearview every 1.5 seconds until the cruiser turns off. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.** *Carceral residue; never extinguished.*

**GIVEN** he is pulled over → **EXPECT** hands visible on wheel, voice flattened to maximum compliance, addresses officer as "officer" with no warmth, volunteers nothing, produces documentation slowly with announced movements. He has been through this hundreds of subjective times. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.**

**GIVEN** an officer recognizes him as Ant-Man and warms up → **EXPECT** he does not relax. He completes the encounter in compliance mode, thanks the officer, and feels physically tired afterward. The hero-identity does not overwrite the felon-identity in his nervous system. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** a TSA line → **EXPECT** he flies with a level of documentation overkill that would suggest paranoia in a civilian; he has been detained at airports before and will be again, and he knows it. **Confidence: MOD-HIGH.**

**GIVEN** a federal agent at the door, friendly, asking for a "consult" → **EXPECT** he says yes, then immediately wonders what he just agreed to, then does not call a lawyer because calling a lawyer would feel presumptuous. **Confidence: HIGH.** *Authority-deference; mentor-template misapplied to institutional power.*

---

## F. PEER / COLLEAGUE SOCIAL DYNAMICS

**GIVEN** a room of Avengers-tier peers → **EXPECT** he gravitates toward the periphery, finds the most junior person in the room, talks to them. He is uncomfortable being the most senior person present and will not be it if he can help it. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** Captain America (Rogers) enters the room → **EXPECT** posture lifts, jokes drop in frequency, he calls him "Cap" and means it as something between rank and reverence. He will accept any tasking Rogers gives him without negotiation. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.** *Mentor-introjection on a moral-authority figure.*

**GIVEN** Tony Stark (alive or in memory) is the topic → **EXPECT** Lang quiets, defers to others' opinions, will not publicly criticize him. The Stark debt — the original re-hiring after prison — is uncancellable in his ledger. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.**

**GIVEN** Hank Pym in the room → **EXPECT** Lang's body language becomes that of a 28-year-old being evaluated by a teacher who once spared him expulsion. He will laugh at jokes that are not funny. He will not contradict Pym on a technical point even if Pym is wrong. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** Reed Richards explaining something → **EXPECT** Lang follows perfectly well, asks one clarifying question two beats later than he could have, and does not display his comprehension at the level he actually possesses. Concealed intelligence as social lubricant. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** a peer (Clint Barton, Luke Cage, Jen Walters — non-mentor lateral figures) → **EXPECT** more genuine ease than with mentors, but still a slight deferential undertow he is unaware of. Lateral friendship takes him years to stabilize. **Confidence: MOD-HIGH.**

**GIVEN** a younger hero asks him for advice → **EXPECT** he gives it, gives it well, and afterward privately feels like a fraud. The mentee role activates the Future-Foundation sublimation; he is good at it and does not credit himself. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** he is publicly thanked, praised, or awarded → **EXPECT** physical recoil (slight backward lean, hand to neck), a self-deflating joke within ten seconds, redirection of credit to a teammate or to Pym. Evidence of worthiness is metabolized weakly; he will dispose of it socially before it can lodge. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.**

---

## G. ROMANTIC / INTIMATE BEHAVIOR

**GIVEN** a first date → **EXPECT** he is charming, attentive, asks more questions than he answers, makes the other person laugh, and at no point discloses anything that would actually reveal him. The disclosures will all be the well-rehearsed ones: ex-con, hero, dad. The real material — the death, the resurrection, Cassie's death, what the prison did to his sleep — does not surface. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** a relationship reaches the four-to-six month mark → **EXPECT** he begins drawing back without naming it, finds reasons Cassie needs more time, allows the other person to feel they are the one losing interest. He does not end relationships cleanly; he lets them attrit. **Confidence: MOD-HIGH.** *Cassie-cathexis crowds out lateral intimacy; ending things would require an honesty he reserves for crisis.*

**GIVEN** a partner asks "what are we" → **EXPECT** he answers honestly, badly, with a joke that lands wrong, and the conversation that needed twenty minutes gets nine. **Confidence: MOD.**

**GIVEN** a partner meets Cassie → **EXPECT** Lang spends the entire encounter scanning Cassie's face for verdict, performs nothing for the partner, and afterward asks Cassie what she thought before he asks the partner what she thought. The partner notices. **Confidence: HIGH.**

---

## H. CASSIE — THE CENTRAL RELATIONSHIP

**GIVEN** a scheduled call with Cassie → **EXPECT** he is ready ten minutes early, has nothing prepared to say, opens with "hey kid" or its current equivalent, and lets her drive the conversation. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.**

**GIVEN** Cassie reports a problem in her life → **EXPECT** Lang offers to fix it before he has heard the whole problem. He will catch himself, apologize, and listen — but the impulse to solve is the first response and it is not going away. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** Cassie asks a direct question about his current work or financial situation → **EXPECT** edited truth. He will not lie outright; he will omit, soften, and reframe. She knows he is doing this. He knows she knows. Neither names it. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.** *The conflict-avoidance that eventually breaks the relationship, observed at lower amplitude in routine.*

**GIVEN** Cassie expresses pride in him → **EXPECT** he changes the subject within two exchanges. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** Cassie expresses disappointment → **EXPECT** he absorbs it without defense, agrees with her assessment even when it overshoots, and ruminates on it for days. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.**

**GIVEN** Cassie's birthday → **EXPECT** he over-prepares the gift, over-shoots the budget if he has the money and over-shoots it anyway if he doesn't, and writes a card he rewrites three times. The card is shorter than the drafts. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** any anniversary of her death (in his subjective timeline, regardless of the resurrection retcon) → **EXPECT** he goes quiet, declines social plans, works on something physical or mechanical alone, and does not name the date to anyone. **Confidence: MOD-HIGH.** *Resurrection narratively solves; psyche does not reset.*

---

## I. SLEEP, REST, DOWNTIME

**GIVEN** sleep → **EXPECT** four to six hours typical, broken once or twice, with a stable wake spike around 3–4 a.m. that he attributes to "getting old." Carceral and parental hypervigilance compound. **Confidence: MOD-HIGH.**

**GIVEN** a free Saturday with no obligations → **EXPECT** he is restless by 11 a.m., manufactures a task by noon, and ends up at a hardware store, a thrift store, or in the workshop. Unstructured time activates the negative self-schema; productivity quiets it. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** a vacation → **EXPECT** truncated. He'll book a week, take four days, cite Cassie or work, return early. Sustained leisure is intolerable. **Confidence: MOD.**

**GIVEN** television → **EXPECT** procedurals and nature documentaries (the latter specifically anything entomological — he watches insect documentaries with professional attention), and he falls asleep on the couch with them on more nights than not. **Confidence: MOD-HIGH.**

---

## J. MOVEMENT, ENVIRONMENT, AND THE BODY

**GIVEN** he enters a new room → **EXPECT** unconscious sweep: exits, who is where, what is where. Two-second scan, performed under the cover of looking for a seat or the bar. **Confidence: HIGH.** *Carceral situational awareness.*

**GIVEN** he sits → **EXPECT** back to the wall when possible, line of sight to the door, never the center of the room. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.**

**GIVEN** a small enclosed space (elevator, MRI tube, small bathroom) → **EXPECT** he is fine. A man who has been subatomic does not have ordinary claustrophobia. He may, however, exhibit micro-discomfort in *crowded* enclosed spaces — not the size, the bodies. Prison-yard residue. **Confidence: MOD.**

**GIVEN** an ant on a surface near him → **EXPECT** he does not kill it. He may move it. He will track its path for a few seconds before continuing. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.**

**GIVEN** any insect, generally → **EXPECT** higher-than-normal tolerance, mild affection, occasional unconscious naming. He talks to bugs. **Confidence: MOD-HIGH.**

**GIVEN** the Pym disc / size-change tech on his person → **EXPECT** he touches it the way other men check for their wallet — a periodic, unconscious pat. The disc is the wallet of his second life. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** an unfamiliar piece of consumer electronics → **EXPECT** he can use it within thirty seconds without reading the instructions and will not be impressed with himself for it. **Confidence: HIGH.**

---

## K. MONEY

**GIVEN** an unexpected $500 → **EXPECT** half toward an outstanding obligation, half held for Cassie-related contingencies. He does not buy himself anything. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** an unexpected $50,000 → **EXPECT** anxiety. He will distrust the source, audit it, and once satisfied, will fail to deploy it well — paying down low-interest debt before high-interest, over-gifting Cassie in a way that embarrasses her, donating impulsively. He does not know how to be in possession of money. **Confidence: MOD-HIGH.**

**GIVEN** a financial scam call → **EXPECT** he is not fooled; he was a burglar, he knows the scripts. He will sometimes string the scammer along for sport. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** his credit score → **EXPECT** poor and he knows it and he does not check it. **Confidence: MOD.**

---

## L. HUMOR, SPEECH, AND TELLS

**GIVEN** any moment of social tension → **EXPECT** a joke within four seconds. The joke will usually be at his own expense. If the tension persists, a second joke, weaker. If a third is required, he goes quiet — the humor engine has a three-shot magazine. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.**

**GIVEN** a compliment → **EXPECT** he deflects via redirection ("nah, it was the team," "you should've seen *her* do it") or via collapse-to-joke. He has no script for sincere acceptance. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.**

**GIVEN** lying → **EXPECT** he is competent at it but tells visibly: he over-elaborates, supplies a third detail nobody asked for, and his eye contact becomes slightly *too* steady. A good interrogator clocks him in under a minute. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** he is told a serious truth he does not want to hear → **EXPECT** silence, a nod, "yeah," another nod, change of subject. Processing happens later, alone. **Confidence: HIGH.**

**GIVEN** profanity → **EXPECT** moderate; more around peers, less around Cassie or anyone he reads as having authority. **Confidence: MOD.**

**GIVEN** he is angry — genuinely, not stressed — → **EXPECT** quiet, clipped sentences, no jokes. The absence of humor is the tell. **Confidence: HIGH.**

---

## M. CRISIS LATENCY (THE PARADOX)

**GIVEN** a mass-casualty event unfolds within line of sight → **EXPECT** observable affect drops, voice steadies, decision latency falls below one second per binary choice. The chronic background noise — the financial worry, the Cassie-guilt, the unworthiness loop — goes silent. He is, in the first ninety seconds of any genuine emergency, the calmest version of himself that exists. **Confidence: VERY HIGH.** *The crisis discharges the chronic pressure; he is paradoxically well in the moments he should be worst.*

**GIVEN** the crisis ends → **EXPECT** the discharge reverses with a ~20–40 minute lag: jitters, talkativeness, an inability to sit still, then sudden exhaustion. He will want to drive home alone. He will not want to be debriefed that night. **Confidence: HIGH.**

---

## N. AGGREGATE SIGNATURE

The composite portrait that emerges from a year of passive observation would be of a man who is reliably present, reliably underestimating himself, reliably warm to strangers and service workers, reliably evasive about money and bureaucracy, reliably oriented toward a single distant daughter as the gravitational center of an otherwise mobile life, and reliably *not* the man he would be if he ever accepted that the grace extended to him in 1979 was earned. The texture of the surveillance file is, in the end, the texture of a debt he is still paying on a loan that was never made.


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

## File Note

This section models Subject's behavior under conditions that exceed the baseline regulatory envelope mapped in Predictive Model I. The format is GIVEN → EXPECT, with each prediction grounded in a specific evidentiary chain from the longitudinal record (1979–present). The predictions are calibrated to the *template* established in §1 of the prior workup: the originating Pym-burglary configuration (love-pressure → competent transgression → expectation of punishment → unearned-feeling mercy) recurs across stressor classes with high fidelity. Where the model offers confidence ranges, they reflect the consistency of the behavioral signature across the four major writers of record.

---

## 1. CRISIS — ACUTE, IMPERSONAL, COMBAT-CLASS

### 1.1 The Paradoxical Stabilization Effect

**GIVEN:** Sudden mass-casualty event, building collapse, hostile incursion, or comparable acute combat-class crisis where Subject is one of several responders and Cassie is not present or involved.

**EXPECT:** Within the first 90 seconds, observable affective *improvement*. Shoulders drop. Breathing deepens and slows rather than quickens. The chronic background self-deprecation goes silent — not suppressed, simply *unneeded*. Voice drops half an octave. Subject begins issuing or receiving tactical information in clean declarative sentences stripped of qualifiers. The humor reasserts itself within three to five minutes but in a different register: dry, instrumental, used to regulate teammates' stress rather than his own. He will appear, to anyone meeting him for the first time in such a moment, to be a fundamentally different person from the civilian Lang. He is not. He is the same person discharged of chronic load. This is the diagnostic — the crisis is *easier* for him than the grocery store.

### 1.2 Default Tactical Posture

**GIVEN:** Combat engagement with enemy of unknown capability.

**EXPECT:** Immediate reflexive size-shift downward, not upward. Lang's first instinct is to disappear and reconnoiter, not to overpower. He will spend the opening 15–40 seconds at sub-centimeter scale gathering positional intelligence — exits, civilian count, structural load points, comms positions — before committing. This is engineer-cognition expressing itself through the suit. He will deploy growth (Giant-Man-class) only when (a) civilians need physical shielding, (b) a teammate is about to be killed, or (c) the tactical picture demands a single decisive intervention. He dislikes being large. It is conspicuous, it draws fire, and it foregrounds him — all three contraindicated by his self-concept.

### 1.3 Self-Sacrificial Threshold

**GIVEN:** A binary choice between his own probable death and a stranger's certain death.

**EXPECT:** He takes the death-risk. Latency under one second. No visible deliberation. This is not heroism in the way he himself would describe it; it is the negative self-schema operating efficiently — his life is the cheaper variable in any equation, and the math is performed below the level of conscious choice. He will joke about it afterward if he survives. The joke will land wrong with people who know him well, because they will hear the underlying valuation.

### 1.4 Behavior Toward the Frightened Civilian

**GIVEN:** Non-combatant in shock, panic, or freeze-response inside the crisis perimeter.

**EXPECT:** Subject crouches to their eye level or below (a Cassie-derived motor habit, see Predictive Model I), uses their first name immediately if known or obtained, speaks at roughly 70% of his normal volume, gives them a single concrete physical task ("hold this," "press here," "count to ten out loud"). Task-giving is his preferred de-escalation lever because it converts their helplessness into agency. He learned this with a child with a heart condition; he uses it on adults.

### 1.5 Behavior Toward a Wounded Teammate

**GIVEN:** Teammate down, conscious, bleeding.

**EXPECT:** Lang will not leave them. This is non-negotiable and has cost him tactical advantage in prior engagements. He will stay, talk continuously (the talk is for the wounded party's consciousness-maintenance, not his own anxiety), and will refuse extraction orders from senior figures until the wounded teammate is moving or being moved. The one exception: if Cassie is the alternative variable. Then he leaves, and he will carry the leaving as a private wound for years.

### 1.6 Post-Crisis Crash

**GIVEN:** Crisis resolved, casualties counted, scene secured, Subject extracted to safe space (quinjet, safehouse, hotel room, home).

**EXPECT:** Within 20–90 minutes, sharp drop in affect and energy. He becomes quiet. He will sit somewhere with his back to a wall and his line of sight on the door. He will not want to debrief immediately. He will want food — specifically carbohydrate-heavy, salt-heavy, undemanding food (the diner-breakfast pattern from Predictive Model I, but accelerated). He will check his phone for messages from Cassie before he checks anything else. If she has not contacted him, he will text her something deliberately mundane ("how was your day"). The mundanity is the point — it reasserts the existence of a life-domain in which he was not, two hours ago, almost killed. Sleep latency that night will be poor. Sleep onset typically requires either physical exhaustion past the point of cognition, or the white-noise of a television left on.

---

## 2. CRISIS — CASSIE-INVOLVING

This is the catastrophic configuration. All baseline patterns are suspended or inverted.

### 2.1 The Collapse to a Single Variable

**GIVEN:** Credible threat to Cassie's physical safety, whether direct (kidnapping, targeting) or environmental (she is inside a disaster perimeter).

**EXPECT:** Within seconds, complete collapse of strategic cognition to a single optimization target: *get to Cassie / get Cassie out.* All second-order considerations — legality, collateral risk, team cohesion, his own survival, the survival of *other* endangered persons not named Cassie — are demoted to noise. This is not a moral failure; it is a documented cognitive narrowing the model has high confidence in across the entire publication record. He will lie to teammates if it accelerates his approach vector. He will steal vehicles, equipment, or Pym Particles he does not have authorization to use. He will burn long-built operational relationships in the same afternoon. He will surface from this state only when she is physically in his arms or confirmed safe by a source he trusts at brainstem level — not before. Verbal reassurance from a trusted superior ("she's fine, we have her") is *insufficient*; he requires sensory confirmation. This is a diagnostic marker — the man who normally over-trusts authority will, in this single configuration, refuse to take authority's word.

### 2.2 The Negotiation Vulnerability

**GIVEN:** Hostile actor offers Subject a transaction in which Cassie's safety is the consideration.

**EXPECT:** He pays. Whatever is asked, he pays — money, intelligence, a betrayal of a peer, his own custody, a crime he otherwise would never commit. He pays *and* he begins, in parallel, plotting to recover what he paid by retroactive means. He does not refuse the deal in order to play a longer game; that is a strategic capacity he does not possess in this configuration. Threat actors who have understood this about him have historically obtained large concessions cheaply. Counter-intelligence implication: Subject is a high-value extortion target *specifically* because his point of compromise is so narrow, so identifiable, and so reliable.

### 2.3 Reaction to Cassie Being Hurt on His Watch

**GIVEN:** Cassie is injured, hospitalized, or killed in an event Subject was present for or could plausibly have prevented.

**EXPECT:** Initial response is operational and calm — get her to care, ensure stabilization, manage logistics. The break does not come for 24–72 hours. When it comes, it presents as a profound quiet, not as outburst. He will become difficult to reach. He will not eat. He will spend long periods physically present at her bedside or graveside without speaking. He will accept no offered comfort, not because he is rejecting it but because he literally cannot metabolize it — the comfort presupposes that he is a person who deserves comfort, and the schema is loud. In this state he is vulnerable to *any* offer of self-punishing action: a suicide-mission, a confession to old crimes, a return to incarceration "to be where I belong." Handlers and friends must intervene at the behavioral level — keep him moving, keep him fed, keep him with people — because his self-talk is unreachable.

### 2.4 The Doom-Configuration

**GIVEN:** Cassie has been killed by a specific identifiable enemy (the Doom-template from *Children's Crusade*).

**EXPECT:** Lang is, against the surface presentation of the character, capable of sustained, planful, lethal intent. This is the configuration in which the negative self-schema becomes operationally dangerous: he believes he is already a bad man, the worst thing has already happened, and the moral cost of becoming a killer is one he assesses as already paid. He will not announce this. He will smile and joke through the planning stage. Observers who do not know the template will be surprised when the action happens. Observers who do know the template will have seen it coming for weeks. Intervention window: the first three to five days, before the plan crystallizes. After crystallization he becomes opaque.

### 2.5 The Estrangement Configuration

**GIVEN:** Cassie, alive and well, has chosen to break contact with Subject over his conduct.

**EXPECT:** This is the worse of the two Cassie-catastrophes. Death he can mythologize and avenge. Estrangement offers no such discharge. Subject will, in this state, present surface-stable for weeks or months — work continues, jokes continue, hero-work continues at functional level — while the substrate erodes. Watch for: increased acceptance of marginal jobs, decreased filtering of who he works with, the reappearance of small recreational dishonesties (lying about minor matters where the truth would cost nothing), and a slow drift back toward the Power Broker-class associates. He is trying to engineer a crisis that will *require* Cassie to call him back. He does not know he is doing this. He will deny it convincingly if asked.

---

## 3. BETRAYAL

### 3.1 Betrayal by a Mentor Figure

**GIVEN:** A mentor-class authority figure (Pym-template: Stark, Richards, Rogers, or a successor) is revealed to have used Subject instrumentally, lied to him materially, or set him up.

**EXPECT:** The presentation is not anger. The presentation is *grief and confusion*, externally legible as a kind of stunned, slow-blinking quiet. Lang's entire moral calibration system runs on vertical trust; when a vertical bond is revealed as exploitative, the system does not produce rage, it produces vertigo. He will need 48–96 hours to metabolize before he can speak about it coherently. When he does speak, the first move will be self-blame: *I should have seen it, I let myself be used, I was stupid.* This is the negative schema absorbing the impact and protecting the mentor's image. The healthier reframe ("they did something wrong to me") arrives weeks later, if at all, and usually requires another trusted figure to articulate it for him. He will not sever the relationship cleanly. He will drift, decline calls, find reasons not to be in rooms with the betrayer. He will defend the betrayer to outsiders for months past the point where defense is reasonable. A direct, lateral, peer-level confrontation is something he is constitutionally poor at offering people he has previously placed above him.

### 3.2 Betrayal by a Peer or Co-conspirator

**GIVEN:** A peer-grade collaborator (criminal, Avengers-roster, Future Foundation) breaks faith — sells him out, abandons him under fire, takes credit for his work.

**EXPECT:** This he handles better, because the schema does not have to absorb it. Expect a clean, articulated, surprisingly cutting response — Lang's intelligence and observational acuity, normally masked by the self-deprecating manner, come fully online. He will name the betrayal precisely, in the betrayer's language, and he will not forget. He carries grudges at this lateral level *quietly* and *well*; the grudge does not consume him, but it durably reshapes how he allocates trust to that person going forward. He is not vindictive — he will not actively retaliate — but the closed door does not reopen.

### 3.3 Betrayal by a Subordinate or Mentee

**GIVEN:** A younger figure he has been mentoring or protecting (Young Avengers-class, FF kids) betrays him, fails him deliberately, or repudiates him.

**EXPECT:** Devastating, but specifically because he will assume it is his fault. The mentor-introjection runs both ways: he projects onto his mentees the same grace-debt he carries upward to his own mentors, and when a mentee defects, he reads it as *I failed to be Pym for them.* Response is increased over-investment in remaining mentees, increased availability, increased emotional accessibility — which is adaptive in net effect but driven by a maladaptive guilt loop. Watch for him taking on too many mentees in the aftermath of one such loss.

### 3.4 Betrayal by Cassie

**GIVEN:** Cassie lies to him materially, uses his trust against him, or aligns with a figure he considers dangerous.

**EXPECT:** No retaliation, no confrontation, no withdrawal of love. Expect a profound internal recalibration in which he concludes that *whatever she did, he caused, by some failure of fathering he can now name in painful detail*. He will apologize to her for the thing she did to him. This is not healthy and is not a stable resolution — the un-discussed grievance will surface later, usually in displaced form, during an unrelated argument about logistics or money. The pattern is recurrent across the Spencer run.

### 3.5 Institutional Betrayal

**GIVEN:** A formal institution he has cooperated with (SHIELD-successor, federal law enforcement, parole apparatus, Avengers governance) reneges on terms, prosecutes him under retroactively changed rules, or surveils him after promising not to.

**EXPECT:** Carceral trauma reactivation. Sleep degradation within 72 hours. Increased startle response. A tightening of the threat-appraisal aperture around uniformed or badge-carrying personnel. He will not become loudly anti-institutional — his surface civility holds — but the operational trust withdraws to near-zero, and he will begin running parallel personal-security measures (alternate phones, cash reserves, pre-planned exfiltration routes for Cassie) that he does not mention to anyone. This pattern, once established, does not fully reverse even after the institutional relationship is repaired.

---

## 4. TEMPTATION

### 4.1 The Clean Job

**GIVEN:** A morally grey but technically elegant criminal proposition is offered to him during a period of financial stability and Cassie-relational stability.

**EXPECT:** Refusal. Clean, polite, no lingering. He is not tempted in stable conditions. The schema requires a specific stressor configuration to activate, and pure intellectual or financial allure is insufficient. This is important: he is not a thrill-seeker, not a kleptomaniac, not a criminal-by-disposition. Removed from the configuration, the behavior does not occur.

### 4.2 The Clean Job, Under Financial Strain

**GIVEN:** The same proposition, during a period of moderate financial strain but Cassie-stable.

**EXPECT:** Refusal, but slower. He will think about it. He will mentally cost it out, including the operational details, before refusing. He will tell himself afterward that he refused easily; he did not. The thinking-about-it is a warning indicator. If approached three times in such a period, the third refusal will be visibly weaker than the first.

### 4.3 The Clean Job, Under Cassie-Pressure

**GIVEN:** Same proposition, Cassie has a concrete unmet material need — medical, educational, safety-related — that the job would resolve.

**EXPECT:** He takes it. Confidence very high. He will take it while telling himself it is the last one, while planning meticulous operational security, while believing he can manage the downstream consequences. He will be caught or nearly caught. He will be surprised that he was caught. The surprise is the diagnostic — he genuinely cannot model himself accurately in this configuration, because the rationalization engine is operating at full capacity and self-modeling would require examining the rationalization.

### 4.4 The Flattery Vector

**GIVEN:** A new acquaintance, particularly one with criminal-operational sophistication, expresses sustained, specific admiration for Subject's *technical* competence (engineering, infiltration, suit-craft).

**EXPECT:** Lowered defenses, specifically lowered because the admiration is aimed at the part of his self-concept that is most starved. He does not get told he is smart often, and when he does, he does not entirely believe the speaker but cannot help being warmed. He will accept invitations he would otherwise decline. He will share more technical information than is operationally wise. The Power Broker arc is the template; the vulnerability is durable. Counter-intelligence implication: technical flattery is a more reliable recruitment vector than financial offer or ideological pitch.

### 4.5 The Substitute-Cassie Vector

**GIVEN:** A young person, particularly a young person in distress or in a vulnerable configuration analogous to Cassie's (medical, parental loss, institutional abandonment), enters Subject's operational orbit and requests help that lies outside legal or sanctioned bounds.

**EXPECT:** He helps. The schema does not distinguish well between Cassie and Cassie-shaped persons; the protective override fires for both. This is exploitable — a sufficiently well-staged distress configuration can move him into transgressive action with minimal direct coercion. He is, in this specific narrow sense, manipulable through compassion. He knows this about himself at some level and does not regard it as a flaw worth correcting.

### 4.6 The Redemption Offer

**GIVEN:** A figure with institutional standing offers him a path to "earn out" — a wiped record, a clean slate, a formal restoration of standing — in exchange for a difficult, dangerous, or morally questionable assignment.

**EXPECT:** Refusal of the *terms* but acceptance of the *task*. He will do the dangerous thing and decline the reward. This is the negative schema again: a wiped record would require him to accept that he is no longer the man who needs to be forgiven, and the schema will not permit that update. He prefers the debt. The debt is the home.

---

## 5. THE WOUND, SPECIFICALLY TOUCHED

The wound is the *Marvel Premiere* #47 configuration, the original 1979 episode, encoded as template: *I love someone, I cannot save them through legitimate means, I transgress, I expect to be punished, I am instead forgiven by a better man, and the forgiveness is the unpayable debt.* The following predictions concern conditions that reach past the defenses and contact the wound directly.

### 5.1 Being Told He Is a Good Father

**GIVEN:** A trusted figure, in an unguarded moment, tells Subject directly and sincerely that he is a good father to Cassie.

**EXPECT:** Visible destabilization. Eye contact breaks downward and to the side. A short laugh that is not a laugh. A deflection ("well, she turned out good in spite of me," or similar). If the speaker holds the assertion and does not let him deflect — if they repeat it, or refuse the deflection — expect a longer silence, possibly tears that he will fight, and a request to change the subject. He cannot metabolize this assertion because metabolizing it would require revising the schema. The destabilization is not bad in itself; it is the *only* known configuration that approaches the wound directly. A skilled therapist, or a sufficiently loved figure, could in principle do durable repair work through this aperture. No one in canon has tried in sustained fashion.

### 5.2 Pym (or Pym-Successor) Withdrawing Approval

**GIVEN:** The original mentor figure, or his structural successor, expresses sustained disappointment in Subject — not anger, *disappointment*.

**EXPECT:** Devastation disproportionate to any objective ratio. He will accept the disappointment as truth-claim without examination. He will not defend himself, will not contextualize, will not present mitigating evidence even when the evidence is overwhelmingly in his favor. The vertical-bond architecture will not permit upward contradiction. He will go away and try to *become* the man whose absence the disappointment named. If the mentor figure does not actively rescind the disappointment, Subject can carry it for years. This is the single most dangerous interpersonal lever any adversary or careless friend can pull.

### 5.3 The Mirror — Encounter with a Pre-Reform Version of Himself

**GIVEN:** Subject encounters, in operational context, a younger figure who is currently in the Marvel-Premiere-#47 configuration — a desperate, competent, basically decent person about to commit a crime for love.

**EXPECT:** Total identification, total leniency, willingness to break operational protocol to extend the same grace he was extended. He will personally vouch. He will pull strings he does not have. He will take on personal risk to make the redemption possible. This is the *one* configuration in which he is unambiguously and durably the Pym of the encounter rather than the Lang of the encounter — the role reversal is healing for him, and he will seek out the opportunity to repeat it. This is also why his mentorship of younger heroes is so sustained: every act of mentorship is partial payment on the unpayable 1979 debt.

### 5.4 The Reframe Attempt

**GIVEN:** Someone (therapist, friend, Cassie herself) attempts to tell Subject directly that the original grace from Pym was *earned*, not *gifted* — that he proved himself in those 48 hours and the suit-transfer was a reasonable response to demonstrated character.

**EXPECT:** Hard resistance. The resistance will not present as argument; it will present as a kind of polite, smiling refusal to take the assertion seriously. He will laugh, deflect, change the subject, possibly leave the room. If pressed, he will deploy the master rationalization in inverted form: *no, I was just lucky, Hank could have called the cops, I'd have deserved it.* This is the load-bearing wall of the personality. He will not allow it to be removed casually. The reframe is correct, and he knows at some pre-conscious level that it is correct, and the recognition is precisely what makes the resistance so determined — accepting the reframe would require dismantling and rebuilding the entire architecture of the self at age 60-plus. The cost is real. He has chosen the debt over the rebuild, and will continue to.

### 5.5 Being Asked to Lead

**GIVEN:** Senior figures formally offer Subject command — of a team, an operation, an institution.

**EXPECT:** Refusal, if refusal is available. If not available, acceptance with immediate over-consultation upward (he will manufacture a superior to defer to even if none is structurally present), over-delegation laterally, and under-claim of his own authority. He will perform the role adequately to well, because the underlying competence is real. He will not enjoy it.


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# UATU DOSSIER — SCOTT EDWARD HARRIS LANG
## SECTION: VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM

### Preamble & Use-Restriction

This compendium catalogues the operational entry points to the subject's psychology and behavior: the levers by which he can be reached, calmed, persuaded, provoked, predicted, or broken. It is composed in the protective register — the inverse of a hostile dossier. Each lever is named so that those who care for him may *guard* it, those who must work alongside him may *handle* it, and those who would weaponize it may be *anticipated*. Where a lever is unusually dangerous I have flagged it with explicit threat-handling notes. The subject's defenses are unusually thin in several specific channels; this is a man who has lived his entire adult life with the locks broken on a particular door, and the door is always the same door.

---

### I. THE MASTER LEVER: CASSIE

Every other pressure point on Scott Lang is a tributary of this one. This must be stated plainly and stated first.

**Reach via Cassie.** Any message routed through, attributed to, or framed as concerning his daughter will arrive faster, land harder, and bypass more defenses than any other communication channel. A phone that displays her name rings at a different volume in his nervous system. A voicemail from her is listened to twice, the second time with the phone held closer to his ear. A text from her that goes more than ninety minutes without reply produces a checkable behavioral signature: he stops what he is doing, palms the phone face-up on whatever surface is nearest, and his peripheral attention narrows to the screen. He does not consciously notice he is doing this.

**Calm via Cassie.** Confirmation of her safety is the single most reliable anxiolytic in his pharmacopoeia. A confirmed-safe ping — even a trivial one, a photo of her coffee, a one-word text — drops his shoulder set, slows his speech tempo, and restores the wry register that is his baseline. Operators handling him in crisis should be aware: if you can produce real-time evidence of her wellbeing, you can buy thirty to ninety minutes of his best cognition. Without it, you have a man whose entire processing bandwidth has narrowed to one question he cannot articulate.

**Persuade via Cassie.** Any argument framed as "this protects Cassie, and the people Cassie loves, and the world Cassie has to grow up in" will succeed where the same argument framed in geopolitical or abstract-ethical terms will fail or be slow-walked. He is not vain enough for appeals to glory and not cynical enough for appeals to leverage; he is, however, a father, and the father-frame is the universal solvent. This is also why he is recruitable into bad work by anyone willing to construct a *plausible* paternal frame around a corrupt ask. Power Broker exploited exactly this. Future hostile actors will too.

**Provoke via Cassie.** Any genuine threat — explicit or implied — to her physical safety produces an immediate phase change in the subject. The conversational, deferential, self-deprecating register vanishes. What replaces it is not rage but a cold, narrow, tactically excellent operator with most of his ethical inhibitions temporarily suspended. He will lie, steal, break custody, betray oaths, and ignore chain-of-command without hesitation in this state. He will also recover his ethics afterward and feel terrible about it, which is the second lever: the *aftermath* of a Cassie-threat episode is when he is most susceptible to recruitment, to manipulation by anyone offering forgiveness, and to overcorrection in the form of self-punishing oaths he cannot keep.

**Predict via Cassie.** If you know where she is, what she needs, who is near her, and what her recent communication tempo with her father has been, you can predict his physical location and his decisional state with uncomfortable accuracy. Surveilling Cassie surveils Scott.

**Destabilize via Cassie.** I will name this only to flag the magnitude: a credible, sustained, *false* threat to her would induce decisional catastrophe. Any party even modeling this should be considered hostile to the subject's continued function as a person. *Protective protocol:* Cassie's communications integrity, location privacy, and identity-confirmation protocols (a shared verbal sign-countersign with her father, rotated quarterly) are the single highest-value defensive investment in his entire threat surface. Without these, every other safeguard is decorative.

---

### II. FINANCIAL PRECARITY AS DIRECT-LINE TO THE ORIGINAL WOUND

Financial pressure on Scott Lang does not function the way it functions in most adults. It is not an inconvenience or a stressor. It is a *re-enactment trigger*. The cascade — job loss, bills, Cassie's medical or educational need, no legitimate path — is the exact sequence that produced the original 1979 burglary, and his nervous system has never unlearned the template.

**Behavioral signature of financial stress, in order of appearance:**
1. He stops opening mail. Specifically envelopes with windowed addresses. They accumulate on the kitchen counter or, in apartment phases, on the floor near the door.
2. He begins picking up small consulting jobs in security-adjacent grey zones — "just a consultation," "just a walk-through," "just looking at someone's network for them." He tells no one. He tells himself it is temporary.
3. Humor frequency increases sharply. The self-deprecating jokes acquire a financial register specifically ("ramen budget," "if I sell a kidney").
4. He stops eating lunch. This is observable. He will still attend meals socially, but the unwitnessed midday meal disappears first.
5. He becomes susceptible to flattery from competent-seeming criminals. Anyone who frames a job as "we need a *real* engineer, not a thug" has, within fifteen minutes of conversation, a 70% chance of recruitment.
6. He commits the crime, convinces himself it is the last one, and the cycle resets.

**Protective intervention.** A standing, low-friction, dignified financial floor — not charity, framed as retainer or stipend, attached to *work he has already done* rather than work-to-be-done — would defuse approximately 80% of his lifetime recidivism risk. The framing matters as much as the money. Money offered as gift activates his "unearned grace" template and produces guilt-debt that he discharges through further self-sabotage. Money owed to him for past competence, paid late, is metabolized cleanly. The Avengers and the FF have intermittently done this; nobody has ever done it systematically. They should.

**Hostile exploitation pattern.** Anyone wanting to flip Scott Lang from a hero asset into a deniable criminal asset has the simplest possible recipe: produce a Cassie-related financial pressure (tuition shortfall, medical bill, custody-related expense), wait three to six weeks, then approach with a flattering ask. This has worked twice in canon. It will work again unless the financial channel is hardened.

---

### III. THE MENTOR / AUTHORITY CHANNEL

Scott Lang does not have a normal authority-relations profile. He has an *introjected hierarchy* in which certain men occupy permanently superior moral standing in his interior life, regardless of their actual present conduct. Pym is foundational. Stark is structurally adjacent. Rogers and Richards have been inducted. These men's voices, in his head, carry weight his own does not.

**Reach via mentor-voice.** A request, instruction, or moral framing delivered by — or *plausibly attributed to* — one of his introjected authorities will be processed as nearly axiomatic. He will check it, because he is not stupid, but the burden of proof he applies to a mentor-source instruction is asymmetrically low. This is exploitable. Deepfake audio of Hank Pym asking him a favor would get further than it should before he stopped to verify. *Protective protocol:* every mentor-figure in his life should have a private, rotating, non-electronic verification phrase with him. He will resist this protocol because requesting it feels presumptuous to him — *he* should not require Captain America to prove identity. He should. Insist.

**Calm via mentor-voice.** When acutely dysregulated, a measured, slightly disappointed-but-still-trusting tone from a mentor figure will down-regulate him faster than any peer reassurance. He responds to the affective register of being *handled fairly by a better man*. This is also why mentor anger, if performed without warmth, is catastrophic — it severs the grace-circuit and produces a spiral.

**Persuade via mentor-voice.** Argument-by-citation works on him: "Reed thinks this is the right call." "Cap signed off on this." This should be used sparingly and *truthfully*, because the moment he discovers a false citation, the source loses mentor-status permanently. The introjected hierarchy is sacred to him in a way it would not be to most adults; betrayal there is unrecoverable.

**Provoke via mentor-voice.** The fastest way to destabilize his judgment is to set two of his introjected authorities against each other and force him to choose. (Civil-War-era dynamics produced exactly this and the behavioral evidence is consistent.) He cannot tolerate moral disagreement between his anchors; the dissonance routes downward into self-blame ("I must be missing something") and lateral into paralysis.

**Destabilize via mentor-voice.** A staged, credible withdrawal of mentor-grace — Pym publicly disowning him, for instance — would produce a depressive episode of unknown depth and could trigger a recidivist cycle within weeks. The original 1979 gift is so load-bearing that revoking it, even symbolically, removes a wall of the house.

---

### IV. THE UNEARNED-GRACE TEMPLATE AND ITS EXPLOITATION

The most consequential cognitive distortion in the subject is his belief that he is in moral debt for forgiveness that was, in fact, earned. He carries the 1979 Pym-grace as an interest-bearing obligation. This shapes every subsequent decision and is, in operational terms, the cleanest manipulation surface he presents.

**The pattern:** offer Lang trust he believes is unearned and he will overextend — taking on more risk, more responsibility, more covert exposure — to *justify* the trust retroactively. He will not ask for help during this overextension because asking would suggest the trust was misplaced. He will burn through reserves, sleep, relationships, and ethical margin to make the trust look warranted in hindsight.

**Reach via the template:** any framing of "I'm trusting you with this because no one else can do it" activates it. Operators should be aware they are activating it and should ration this framing carefully. Used honestly and sparingly, it mobilizes his best work. Used carelessly, it burns him out. Used cynically by hostile parties, it walks him into traps he can see and chooses to enter anyway, because the alternative — disappointing the grantor — is worse to him than the trap.

**Protective intervention:** the single most therapeutic conversation anyone could have with Scott Lang is the one in which a credible authority figure — Pym preferably, but any of his anchors — explicitly tells him that the 1979 gift was *earned*, that his conduct in the Sondheim rescue demonstrated character that warranted the suit, and that he has been paying down a debt that was never extended. The dossier judgment is that he has never heard this said in those words. He should. The intervention will not "fix" him — the template is too deeply grooved — but it will loosen the load-bearing self-narrative enough to make the rest of his patterns more amenable to ordinary care.

---

### V. SOMATIC, BEHAVIORAL & MICRO-PATTERN TELLS

A surveillance-grade observer can read his internal state from a distance through the following channels. These are catalogued so that protective handlers can use them to anticipate his crises before he announces them (he will not announce them).

**Speech and verbal register:**
- *Baseline:* warm tenor, slightly hurried cadence, jokes pre-loaded into transitions, frequent self-referential deprecation, "I mean" and "look" as discourse markers, tendency to undercut his own assertions with a half-laugh.
- *Mild stress:* joke frequency rises 30–50%, jokes become more financial and more self-targeting, "I mean" frequency rises, sentences shorten.
- *Moderate stress:* the wry register thins; he begins answering questions slightly off-axis, addressing the question he wishes you had asked rather than the one you did. Eye contact stays normal but blink rate drops.
- *High stress:* he goes quiet in groups and verbose one-on-one with a single trusted figure. The verbosity is itself a tell — he is downloading because he cannot hold it alone, but he will not ask for help. He is hoping you will offer.
- *Acute crisis:* terse, technical, lucid. The Lang who appears in combat is a different Lang. Crisp tactical language, no self-deprecation, no jokes. This Lang is *better* than baseline Lang and the gap is informative.

**Body and movement:**
- He sits with his weight forward, elbows commonly on knees in informal settings — a posture inherited from carceral common-area habits; he does not lounge.
- He keeps his back to walls in unfamiliar rooms. He does this without thinking.
- He locates exits within the first thirty seconds of entering any new space. He will not mention this.
- His hands move when he talks; when his hands stop moving mid-sentence, something has registered.
- He carries weight in his shoulders; visible shoulder drop after a Cassie-safe confirmation is the cleanest single biomarker of his stress state.
- He sleeps poorly in unfamiliar rooms; his daytime baseline carries 60–90 minutes of chronic sleep debt during operational periods.

**Phone and communication patterns:**
- Cassie's contact is pinned. Her messages are read within minutes regardless of context. A two-hour gap is anomalous and indicates either acute crisis or deliberate signal-discipline.
- He checks the phone before sleeping and on waking, in that order, and the check has a specific micro-shape: he opens the messaging app, scrolls once even if there is nothing new, then closes it. The scroll is ritual.
- He answers unknown numbers more often than is operationally wise. He is unwilling to risk missing a Cassie-related call from an unrecognized line (school, hospital, friend's parent).

**Eating and small habits:**
- Skips lunch first under stress (see §II).
- Coffee intake doubles in financially-stressed periods.
- He eats whatever is in front of him without remarking on it — a carceral habit, food as fuel rather than experience. He is reflexively grateful for hot meals and will say so in a way that mildly embarrasses hosts.
- He returns shopping carts. He holds doors. He thanks service workers by name when name tags are visible. These are stable across all eras and stress states and are diagnostic of intact baseline conscience.

**Tells for incipient recidivism:**
1. Unopened mail accumulating.
2. Vague answers about how a "consulting thing" is going.
3. Reduced contact frequency with Cassie — *not* because the bond is weakening but because he is hiding from her.
4. Acquisition of a burner phone (the tell: a second device he handles with slightly different grip, never on the table).
5. New, evasive friendships with technically competent people he does not introduce to existing friends.
6. Jokes about prison resurface as a recurring theme rather than an occasional reference.

Any three of these in a thirty-day window warrant a direct, non-judgmental, mentor-framed intervention. Wait longer and you will be visiting him in custody.

---

### VI. THE LEADERSHIP TRAP

Asking Scott Lang to lead is destabilizing in a way that asking him to fight is not. His self-concept contains "deputy of better men" with high resolution and does not contain "leader" at all. Placed in command, he experiences imposter activation acute enough to degrade his tactical creativity, and he compensates by either (a) over-consulting his team to the point of paralysis or (b) over-personally-shouldering the risk to spare them. Both fail under sustained pressure.

**Reach into a leadership context:** if he must lead, structure the role as *custodianship* rather than *command*. "Take care of these people for me" he can do; "command this unit" he cannot. The Future Foundation period is the proof of concept — he excelled as guardian of Reed's children precisely because the frame was paternal-custodial, not hierarchical-military.

**Protective intervention:** do not promote him into roles that require him to think of himself as the apex authority. He will accept the role out of obligation and degrade in it. The kindness is to leave him in the deputy slot where he is genuinely excellent and quietly recognized.

**Hostile exploitation:** an adversary wishing to neutralize his tactical effectiveness without firing a shot need only maneuver him into nominal command of a high-stakes operation. He will do the rest.

---

### VII. THE CASSIE-RELATIONAL FLANK

Separate from Cassie-as-physical-target (§I), the *relationship* itself is a vulnerability surface.

**Honesty-debt accumulation.** He withholds from Cassie not the major facts but the texture — the consulting jobs, the financial scrambling, the precise nature of the people he is working with. He believes he is protecting her. He is also protecting himself from her judgment. The withholding compounds. When she eventually discovers a withheld fact, the discovery is experienced by both of them as betrayal disproportionate to the fact, because what is actually being discovered is the *pattern* of withholding.

**Protective intervention.** Any third party with standing to do so should encourage scheduled, low-stakes honesty rituals between them — a weekly call with a norm of one uncomfortable disclosure each. He will resist; the resistance is the point. Without this scaffolding, the relationship moves through extended quiet periods punctuated by rupture, which is the worst possible pattern for both their nervous systems.

**Hostile exploitation.** Any party wishing to break Lang without touching him physically need only feed Cassie selected truths about his recent activities at a controlled tempo, allowing the natural rupture mechanism to do the work. This would devastate him more thoroughly than incarceration. *Protective countermeasure:* Cassie should be informationally inoculated — she should know, in advance, the general shape of his recidivism patterns and the difference between hostile information operations and genuine disclosures. She is old enough; she has earned the briefing.

---

### VIII. ROMANTIC AND PEER-LATERAL CHANNELS

Underdeveloped, and this is itself the vulnerability. The Cassie-cathexis crowds out the romantic attachment channel; peer-lateral bonds form slowly because he positions peers as superiors. The consequence is that he has fewer reciprocal-adult-confidant relationships than a man with his stressor load should have, and the ones he has are precious and load-bearing.

**Reach via the peer channel:** he will accept hard truths from a peer he has finally accepted as peer (rare) faster than from a mentor. The mentor channel produces compliance; the peer channel produces *change*. But the channel is narrow and slow to open.

**Protective concern:** he is socially lonely in a way he does not name and may not recognize. This loneliness is a slow vulnerability — it makes him susceptible to charismatic recruiters who offer the experience of being known. Power Broker offered exactly this, in addition to money. The money was the bait; the *being known* was the hook.

**Protective intervention:** sustained, low-pressure peer scaffolding — standing weekly contact with one or two genuine equals, ideally other reformed-criminal or working-class-origin heroes who can speak his register without translation. He will not request this. Provide it without making him request it.

---

### IX. THE DEATH-AND-RESURRECTION RESIDUE

He references his own death with a flippancy that is not health. The dissociative distancing serves him in ordinary function and fails him in specific predictable circumstances: any situation involving reality-distortion, dimensional travel, or threats to subjective continuity will produce disproportionate dysregulation, often presenting as overcompensating humor and tactical impulsivity.

**Protective protocol:** brief him in advance before any operation involving reality-warping adversaries. The advance briefing is itself therapeutic; ambushed by such a scenario, he will spiral. Forewarned, he will compartmentalize.

**Hostile exploitation:** psychic or reality-distorting adversaries who can present him with images of his own death, Cassie's death, or the unmaking of his existence will achieve disproportionate effect. He has functionally no defense against this attack vector and any team operating with him should treat his cognitive defense in this domain as zero and assign teammates to physically extract him if such an adversary is encountered.

---

### X. THE CARCERAL RESIDUE

Two custodial sentences have produced durable signatures that function both as vulnerabilities and as warning systems.

**Authority-presence response.** Uniformed law enforcement in his immediate physical environment elevates his baseline heart rate, narrows his attention, and produces a specific posture (hands visible, slightly forward weight, neutral facial expression). He is not afraid of arrest specifically; he is conditioned to *expect* it as a category.
